**Question:** Michael had always had a large mole on his arm. However, recently he observed changes in its appearance. On the advice of his friend, he visited a dermatologist who biopsied the mole. Which CPT code pertains to the biopsy of a lesion?
Options: {'A': '10040', 'B': '10005', 'C': '10060', 'D': '11100'}

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is a biopsy of a lesion (mole) performed by a dermatologist due to observed changes.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**
**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

*   **CPT 11100:** This code was deleted effective January 1, 2019. Prior to 2019, CPT code 11100 was used to report a biopsy of skin, subcutaneous tissue, and/or mucous membrane, including simple closure, unless otherwise listed. It was used for the first lesion biopsied.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

*   The old definition of CPT 11100 ("Biopsy of skin, subcutaneous tissue and/or mucous membrane") *does* align with the question text, which describes a biopsy of a mole (skin lesion). The match is strong in concept, but it's crucial to acknowledge that this code is no longer valid.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 10040 - Incorrect.** CPT code 10040 is for acne surgery, involving the removal of acne lesions such as comedones, milia, cysts, or pustules. This does not describe the biopsy of a mole.
*   **B: 10005 - Incorrect.** CPT code 10005 is for fine needle aspiration biopsy, including ultrasound guidance, for the first lesion. This is not the appropriate code, as the question does not mention fine needle aspiration, or any type of guidance.
*   **C: 10060 - Incorrect.** CPT code 10060 is for incision and drainage of an abscess, such as a carbuncle, furuncle, or paronychia. This does not describe a biopsy. The scenario involves a mole with changes in appearance, not an abscess.
*   **D: 11100 - Incorrect.** CPT code 11100 was for a biopsy of skin, subcutaneous tissue and/or mucous membrane. **HOWEVER, this code was deleted in 2019**. While it aligns conceptually with the question, it is *no longer a valid code*. As of 2019, biopsies are coded based on the method of removal (tangential, punch, or incisional).

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The *most accurate* answer, conceptually, would have been CPT 11100. However, CPT 11100 was deleted in 2019. As of 2019, the appropriate CPT code should be selected based on the *method* used to perform the biopsy (e.g., tangential, punch, or incisional). Since the question doesn't specify the method, none of the provided options are correct *in the context of 2026 coding guidelines*.

## Question 69 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: What is the purpose of the National Correct Coding Initiative (NCCI)?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
The National Correct Coding Initiative (NCCI) is designed to prevent improper payments by identifying and correcting coding errors, particularly those involving unbundling and inappropriate code combinations. While option A is a broader goal and options C and D are incorrect, option B directly reflects NCCI's core function.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will analyze the medical coding question about the purpose of the National Correct Coding Initiative (NCCI) using the provided guidelines.

**Question:** What is the purpose of the National Correct Coding Initiative (NCCI)?
**Options:** {'A': 'Ensure appropriate coding based on the medical record', 'B': 'Prevent improper payment of procedures that should not be billed together', 'C': 'Assign specific dollar amounts to procedures', 'D': 'Monitor fraudulent billing practices across states'}

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core concept here is the *National Correct Coding Initiative (NCCI)* and its purpose within medical coding and billing.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**
Since the question relates to a policy/initiative rather than a specific CPT/ICD code, I will research the NCCI definition and relate it to the options.

**3. & 4. Deleted Codes:**
The question and options do not refer to any specific deleted codes. Therefore, this step is not applicable.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect:**

*   **A: 'Ensure appropriate coding based on the medical record'**:  The NCCI does contribute to appropriate coding by providing guidelines and edits. It aims to improve accuracy in claims processing. However, this is a broader goal and not the primary, most direct purpose of the NCCI.
*   **B: 'Prevent improper payment of procedures that should not be billed together'**: This is the **most accurate** answer. The NCCI's core function is to identify and prevent incorrect coding combinations and unbundling of services, which directly leads to preventing improper payments. This is achieved through Procedure to Procedure (PTP) edits and Medically Unlikely Edits (MUEs).
*   **C: 'Assign specific dollar amounts to procedures'**: This is incorrect. The NCCI does not assign dollar amounts to procedures. That is the responsibility of other entities and processes involved in healthcare reimbursement.
*   **D: 'Monitor fraudulent billing practices across states'**: While the NCCI's edits can help *identify* potential fraudulent activities, its primary goal is not to actively monitor fraud across states. It's a tool used in preventing improper payments, which *can* be related to fraud, but monitoring fraud is a separate function.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The National Correct Coding Initiative (NCCI), developed by CMS, focuses on preventing improper payments by detecting and correcting coding errors, specifically those related to unbundling and inappropriate code combinations. While the NCCI contributes to overall coding accuracy and can indirectly aid in identifying potential fraud, its core purpose is to ensure correct coding and prevent inappropriate payments for services billed together. Therefore, option B is the most direct and accurate answer.

## Question 71 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Sophia went to a dermatologist for a facial consultation. The doctor noticed a milia near her eye and removed it. Which CPT code represents the removal of milia?

**Selected**: C
**Correct Answer**: C
**Rationale**:
CPT code 10040 is the correct answer because it specifically includes the removal of multiple milia. While other codes might involve removal of lesions, 10040 is the most accurate as milia removal is explicitly mentioned in the code description. The update to CPT 10040 in 2026, changing 'Acne surgery' to 'Extraction', further validates this choice.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about milia removal, following the provided guidelines.

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is the removal of a milia. A milia is a small, white bump typically found on the skin, often around the eyes. The question specifies removal, so the CPT code should reflect an excision or removal procedure.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use search queries to find the definitions of each CPT code option for the current year (2026) and check for any historical changes or deletions.

Based on the search results:

*   **10021 - Fine needle aspiration biopsy, without imaging guidance; first lesion:** This code is for a fine needle aspiration biopsy (FNA), which involves using a thin needle to extract a small sample of tissue or fluid for examination. This is typically a *diagnostic* procedure.
*   **10030 - Image-guided fluid collection drainage by catheter (e.g., abscess, hematoma, seroma, lymphocele, cyst), soft tissue (e.g., extremity, abdominal wall, neck), percutaneous:** This code describes draining a fluid collection with a catheter inserted percutaneously (through the skin) using imaging guidance. Examples include abscesses, hematomas, seromas, or cysts. Moderate sedation may be included.
*   **10040 - Acne surgery (e.g., marsupialization, opening or removal of multiple milia, comedones, cysts, pustules):** This code is for acne surgery, involving procedures like marsupialization, opening, or removal of multiple acne lesions, including milia, comedones, cysts, and pustules. It falls under incision and drainage procedures on the skin. In 2026, the code description was revised to "Extraction (eg, marsupialization, opening or removal of multiple milia, comedones, cysts, pustules)".
*   **10120 - Incision and removal of foreign body, subcutaneous tissues; simple:** This code is for the incision and removal of a foreign body located in the subcutaneous tissues. It is considered a simple procedure.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

None of the codes appear to be deleted for 2026. CPT code 10040 has a minor description change.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable, as there are no deleted codes in this scenario.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 10021 - Incorrect.** This code is for a *diagnostic* fine needle aspiration biopsy. The question specifies *removal* of the milia, not a biopsy.
*   **B: 10030 - Incorrect.** This code is for draining a fluid collection using a catheter with imaging guidance. Milia are small, solid cysts, not fluid collections requiring catheter drainage.
*   **C: 10040 - Correct.** This code is specifically for acne surgery, which includes the removal of milia. The description includes "removal of multiple milia".
*   **D: 10120 - Incorrect.** This code is for the removal of a *foreign body*. Milia are skin lesions, not foreign objects.

**Research Note:**

The key to this question lies in understanding the definitions of the CPT codes. While "incision and drainage" or "removal" might seem like general terms, the specific codes have very different applications. CPT 10040 is the best fit because it explicitly includes "removal of multiple milia" in its description. The 2026 update to CPT 10040 changes "Acne surgery" to "Extraction," which further supports its applicability to the scenario.

## Question 73 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: According to the ICD-10-CM guidelines, when a patient has both an acute and chronic condition, which one should be sequenced first?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
According to the ICD-10-CM Official Guidelines for Coding and Reporting, when a patient has both an acute and chronic condition and there are separate codes for each, the acute condition is generally sequenced first. Therefore, 'Acute condition' is the correct answer.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the ICD-10-CM sequencing guidelines for acute and chronic conditions and determine the correct answer.

Research Note:
The ICD-10-CM Official Guidelines for Coding and Reporting (FY 2026) state the rules for sequencing diagnoses. It's important to consult the official guidelines for the most accurate and up-to-date information. Several sources confirm that when a patient has both an acute and a chronic condition and there are separate codes for each, the acute condition is generally sequenced first.

Answer Breakdown:

*   **A: Acute condition:** This is the correct answer. According to the ICD-10-CM guidelines, the acute condition should be sequenced first.
*   **B: Chronic condition:** This is incorrect. The chronic condition is generally sequenced after the acute condition.
*   **C: Either - based on the severity:** This is incorrect. While severity is a factor in code selection, the sequencing guideline specifically addresses acute and chronic conditions.
*   **D: The condition that is being treated during the visit:** This is incorrect. While the reason for the encounter is important, the acute condition takes precedence when both acute and chronic conditions exist and have separate codes.

Final Answer:
**A: Acute condition**

**3. Analysis of Options:**

*   **A: Inflammation of the liver:** Incorrect. Inflammation of the liver is referred to as hepatitis.
*   **B: Enlargement of the liver:** Correct. This is the definition of hepatomegaly.

**Correct Answer**: D

The correct CPT code for the removal of a skin tag is 11200. This code is specifically designated for this procedure. The other options describe procedures that are not relevant to the removal of a skin tag, such as aspiration (10021), drainage of fluid collections (10030), or incision and drainage of abscesses (10060).

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the removal of a skin tag and provide a detailed explanation of the correct CPT code.

**Question:** During her beach vacation, Lisa noticed a skin tag on her neck. Wanting to wear her new necklace without any obstructions, she decided to visit a dermatologist to have it removed. Which CPT code represents the removal of a skin tag?
Options: {'A': '10021', 'B': '10030', 'C': '10060', 'D': '11200'}

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is the removal of a skin tag. The location is the neck, but the key is the procedure itself.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use online resources to verify the CPT code definitions for 2026 (and prior years if necessary).

**CPT Code Definitions:**

*   **10021:** Fine needle aspiration biopsy, without imaging guidance; first lesion. This involves using a fine needle to collect cells or fluid from a lesion for examination.
*   **10030:** Image-guided fluid collection drainage by catheter (e.g., abscess, hematoma, seroma, lymphocele, cyst), soft tissue (e.g., extremity, abdominal wall, neck), percutaneous. This code is for draining a fluid collection using a catheter inserted through the skin, with imaging guidance.
*   **10060:** Incision and drainage of abscess (e.g., carbuncle, suppurative hidradenitis, cutaneous or subcutaneous abscess, cyst, furuncle, or paronychia); simple or single. This code is for incising and draining an abscess or similar collection of pus.
*   **11200:** Removal of skin tags, multiple fibrocutaneous tags, any area. This code is used for the removal of up to 15 skin tags. If more than 15 skin tags are removed, 11201 is used for each additional 10 skin tags removed.

None of the codes listed are deleted.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable, as no codes are deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 10021 - Incorrect.** This code is for fine needle aspiration, which is a biopsy procedure to collect cells or fluid. The scenario describes removal of the skin tag, not a biopsy.
*   **B: 10030 - Incorrect.** This code describes the drainage of a fluid collection (abscess, hematoma, etc.) by inserting a catheter with image guidance. Skin tag removal is not a fluid drainage procedure.
*   **C: 10060 - Incorrect.** This code is for incision and drainage of an abscess, cyst, or similar infected collection. A skin tag is not an abscess or infected cyst.
*   **D: 11200 - Correct.** This code specifically describes the removal of skin tags. The question describes the removal of a skin tag, making this the correct code.

**Research Note:**

The correct CPT code for the removal of a skin tag is 11200. This code is specifically designated for this procedure. The other options describe procedures that are not relevant to the removal of a skin tag, such as aspiration, drainage of fluid collections, or incision and drainage of abscesses.

The core procedure is cauterization of a bleeding vessel in the nasal cavity to stop persistent nosebleeds (epistaxis).

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use the search tool to find the definitions of the CPT codes provided.

**CPT Code Definitions and Analysis:**

*   **A: 30000** - Incision of nose with aspiration of abscess or hematoma. This code describes the drainage of a lesion, abscess, or hematoma within the nasal cavity. *Incorrect.* This does not describe cauterization of a bleeding vessel.
*   **B: 30901** - Control nasal hemorrhage, anterior, simple (limited cautery and/or packing) any method. This code is for controlling a simple, anterior nosebleed using limited cautery or packing. *Correct.* This accurately describes the procedure of cauterizing a bleeding vessel in the nasal cavity to stop a nosebleed.
*   **C: 31231** - Nasal endoscopy, diagnostic, unilateral or bilateral (separate procedure). This code describes a *diagnostic* nasal endoscopy, where an endoscope is used to examine the nasal passages. It is not appropriate when a therapeutic procedure like cauterization is performed. *Incorrect.* The question describes a *therapeutic* intervention (cauterization), not just a diagnostic examination.
*   **D: 31237** - Nasal/sinus endoscopy, surgical; with biopsy, polypectomy or debridement (separate procedure). This code is for a *surgical* nasal endoscopy that includes a biopsy, polypectomy, or debridement. *Incorrect*. While an endoscope *could* be used to visualize the cauterization site, 30901 is more specific. Furthermore, the question does not mention a biopsy, polypectomy, or debridement.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

None of the codes appear to be deleted.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable, as none of the codes are deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 30000 (Incorrect)**: This code is for drainage of a nasal lesion or abscess, not for cauterizing a bleeding vessel.
*   **B: 30901 (Correct)**: This code accurately describes the procedure performed: control of an anterior nosebleed using cautery.
*   **C: 31231 (Incorrect)**: This code is for a diagnostic nasal endoscopy only, not when a therapeutic procedure is performed.
*   **D: 31237 (Incorrect)**: This code includes surgical endoscopy with biopsy, polypectomy, or debridement, which are not mentioned in the question.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The key to this question is to differentiate between diagnostic and therapeutic procedures, and to select the most specific code. While an endoscope *could* be used, code 30901 specifically describes the *cauterization* of a nosebleed, making it the most accurate choice.

## Question 79 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: After experiencing rapid heartbeats, Karen underwent an electrophysiology study. Which CPT code pertains to this procedure?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
CPT code 93620 (Comprehensive electrophysiologic evaluation including insertion and repositioning of multiple electrode catheters with induction or attempted induction of arrhythmia; with right atrial pacing and recording, right ventricular pacing and recording, His bundle recording) is the most appropriate choice. The question describes an electrophysiology study performed after the patient experienced rapid heartbeats, implying the possibility of arrhythmia. Although not explicitly stated, it is reasonable to assume that the study would involve attempting to induce or evaluate the arrhythmia. While 93619 exists for studies without attempted induction, the clinical context suggests 93620 as the best fit. Codes 93621 and 93622 are add-on codes used in conjunction with a primary procedure and are not appropriate on their own.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question regarding the electrophysiology study, considering the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines.

**Question:** After experiencing rapid heartbeats, Karen underwent an electrophysiology study. Which CPT code pertains to this procedure?
Options: {'A': '93619', 'B': '93620', 'C': '93621', 'D': '93622'}

**Task Breakdown:**
1.  **Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:** Electrophysiology (EP) study for rapid heartbeats (arrhythmia).
2.  **Verify each option against CPT definitions (current AND historical).**
3.  **If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**
4.  **CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**
5.  **Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

**Analysis of Options:**

*   **93619:** *Comprehensive electrophysiologic evaluation with right atrial pacing and recording, right ventricular pacing and recording, His bundle recording, including insertion and repositioning of multiple electrode catheters, without induction or attempted induction of arrhythmia*. This code describes a comprehensive EP study *without* induction of arrhythmia.
*   **93620:** *Comprehensive electrophysiologic evaluation including insertion and repositioning of multiple electrode catheters with induction or attempted induction of arrhythmia; with right atrial pacing and recording, right ventricular pacing and recording, His bundle recording*. This code describes a comprehensive EP study *with* induction or attempted induction of arrhythmia.
*   **93621:** *Comprehensive electrophysiologic evaluation including insertion and repositioning of multiple electrode catheters with induction or attempted induction of arrhythmia; with left atrial pacing and recording from coronary sinus or left atrium (List separately in addition to code for primary procedure)*. This is an add-on code used in conjunction with a primary procedure (like 93620) when left atrial pacing and recording from the coronary sinus or left atrium is performed.
*   **93622:** *Comprehensive electrophysiologic evaluation including insertion and repositioning of multiple electrode catheters with induction or attempted induction of arrhythmia; with left ventricular pacing and recording (List separately in addition to code for primary procedure)*. This is also an add-on code, used when left ventricular pacing and recording is performed.

**Determining the Correct Answer:**

The question states Karen underwent an electrophysiology study after experiencing rapid heartbeats. While the question doesn't explicitly state that arrhythmia was induced, the fact that she experienced rapid heartbeats suggests the *attempt* to induce or evaluate the arrhythmia. Since the question does not specify left atrial or ventricular pacing, 93621 and 93622 are less appropriate.

**Therefore, the best answer is B: 93620.**

**Rationale for Correct/Incorrect Options:**

*   **A: 93619 - Incorrect.** This code is for EP studies *without* induction or attempted induction of arrhythmia, which is less likely given the context of rapid heartbeats.
*   **B: 93620 - Correct.** This code describes a comprehensive EP study *with* induction or attempted induction of arrhythmia, which aligns with the scenario of evaluating rapid heartbeats.
*   **C: 93621 - Incorrect.** This is an add-on code for *left atrial* pacing and recording. The question doesn't provide enough information to justify the use of this add-on code.
*   **D: 93622 - Incorrect.** This is an add-on code for *left ventricular* pacing and recording. The question doesn't provide enough information to justify the use of this add-on code.

**Research Note for Evaluator:**

The selection of CPT code 93620 hinges on the assumption that an electrophysiology study for rapid heartbeats (likely arrhythmia) would involve an attempt to induce or evaluate the arrhythmia during the procedure. While not explicitly stated, this is a reasonable clinical assumption. If the study specifically documented *no* attempt to induce arrhythmia, 93619 would be more appropriate. CPT 2026 changes were reviewed, and no code deletions were identified that would impact the accuracy of this answer.

Options: {'A': 'Low blood sugar level', 'B': 'Normal blood sugar level', 'C': 'High blood sugar level', 'D': 'Blood without sugar'}

The core diagnosis is "hyperglycemia," which relates to the level of glucose in the blood.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

Since the question is about a definition, CPT codes are not directly relevant. ICD-10 codes are used for diagnoses, and while there isn't a direct ICD-10 definition, the term is widely understood within the medical field. I will use medical dictionaries and resources to verify the definition.

Based on the search results:

*   **Hyperglycemia** is defined as a higher than normal level of glucose (sugar) in the blood. It often affects people with diabetes. A fasting blood glucose level greater than 125 mg/dL is generally considered hyperglycemia.
*   **ICD-10:** The most common code is R73.9 (Hyperglycemia, unspecified). More specific codes exist if the hyperglycemia is due to diabetes (e.g., E11.65 for type 2 diabetes with hyperglycemia) or other underlying conditions.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

*   **A: Low blood sugar level** - **Incorrect.** This is the definition of *hypoglycemia*, not hyperglycemia.
*   **B: Normal blood sugar level** - **Incorrect.** Hyperglycemia specifically refers to *high* blood sugar.
*   **C: High blood sugar level** - **Correct.** This is the definition of hyperglycemia.
*   **D: Blood without sugar** - **Incorrect.** While too much sugar is problematic, blood always contains some glucose. "Blood without sugar" isn't a recognized medical term or condition.

**Research Note:**

The question tests the basic definition of "hyperglycemia." While ICD-10 coding guidelines were reviewed, the core of the question relies on medical terminology rather than coding specifics. The correct answer is "High blood sugar level," as supported by multiple medical definitions.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about iron-deficiency anemia secondary to chronic blood loss, using the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines, and provide a concise research note.

**Research Note:**

The question asks for the appropriate ICD-10-CM code for iron-deficiency anemia secondary to chronic blood loss. The 2026 ICD-10-CM code book is effective from October 1, 2025.

*   **Core Diagnosis:** Iron-deficiency anemia secondary to chronic blood loss.

Now, let's evaluate the options:

*   **A: D50.0:** This code is for "Iron deficiency anemia secondary to blood loss (chronic)". This matches the diagnosis exactly.
*   **B: D50.1:** This code is for "Sideropenic dysphagia". This is a specific type of iron deficiency anemia associated with difficulty swallowing and is not a general code for anemia secondary to blood loss.
*   **C: D50.8:** This code is for "Other iron deficiency anemias". This code is used when the iron deficiency anemia does not fit into the other categories like D50.0 or D50.1.
*   **D: D50.9:** This code is for "Iron deficiency anemia, unspecified". This code is used when the cause of the iron deficiency anemia is not specified.

*   **A: D50.0 (Correct):** This is the correct code because it specifically describes iron deficiency anemia secondary to chronic blood loss.

*   **C: D50.8 (Incorrect):** This code is for other types of iron deficiency anemia that are not specifically due to chronic blood loss or sideropenic dysphagia.
*   **D: D50.9 (Incorrect):** This code is used when the cause of the iron deficiency is not specified. Since the question specifies chronic blood loss as the cause, this code is not appropriate.

**Final Answer:**

The appropriate ICD-10-CM code for Julie's diagnosis of iron-deficiency anemia secondary to chronic blood loss is **A: D50.0**.

**Question**: Dr. Harris diagnosed Grace with hyperthyroidism and recommended a partial thyroidectomy. Which CPT code describes this procedure?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
Based on the research, none of the options are a perfect fit. However, following the principle of selecting the least incorrect option and considering that the question mentions a 'partial thyroidectomy' without specifying laterality or the extent of the procedure, code 60210 (Partial thyroid lobectomy, unilateral; with or without isthmusectomy) is the most appropriate choice. While the question does not explicitly state 'unilateral', 60210 is the closest description of a partial removal of thyroid tissue. The other options involve either a biopsy (60100), which is incorrect because the question describes a partial thyroidectomy (resection), or subtotal/total lobectomy, which is more extensive than a partial thyroidectomy.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the partial thyroidectomy, providing detailed explanations for each option and a research note.

Based on my research of CPT and ICD-10 guidelines for 2026, here's an analysis of the provided options:

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

*   **Procedure:** Partial thyroidectomy
*   **Diagnosis:** Hyperthyroidism

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

*   **A: 60210 - Partial thyroid lobectomy, unilateral; with or without isthmusectomy**
    *   This code describes the partial removal of one lobe of the thyroid gland, with or without removing the isthmus (the connecting part between the lobes).
*   **B: 60212 - Partial thyroid lobectomy, unilateral; with contralateral subtotal lobectomy, including isthmusectomy**
    *   This code describes the partial removal of one thyroid lobe along with a *subtotal* (less than total) removal of the opposite lobe, including the isthmus.
*   **C: 60100 - Biopsy thyroid, percutaneous core needle**
    *   This code is for a *biopsy* of the thyroid, specifically a percutaneous core needle biopsy, where a tissue sample is taken for examination. This is a diagnostic procedure, not a therapeutic removal of thyroid tissue.
*   **D: 60225 - Total thyroid lobectomy, unilateral; with contralateral subtotal lobectomy, including isthmusectomy**
    *  This code describes the *total* removal of one thyroid lobe along with a *subtotal* (less than total) removal of the opposite lobe, including the isthmus.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

*   None of the codes appear to be deleted for 2026.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

*   Not applicable, as no codes are deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 60210 - Incorrect.** This describes a partial removal of *only one* lobe. The question implies a partial thyroidectomy without specifying how much of the thyroid is removed. Without knowing how much is removed and if the isthmus is removed, you can't assume that only one lobe is partially removed.
*   **B: 60212 - Incorrect.** This describes a partial removal of one lobe AND a subtotal removal of the other lobe including the isthmus. The question asks for a *partial thyroidectomy*, which means a portion of the thyroid is removed, but doesn't specify one or both lobes.
*   **C: 60100 - Incorrect.** This is a *biopsy* code, not a code for the *removal* of thyroid tissue (thyroidectomy).
*   **D: 60225 - Incorrect.** This describes a *total* removal of one lobe and a subtotal removal of the other lobe, including the isthmus. The question asks for a *partial* thyroidectomy.

**Correct Answer:**

Based strictly on the information provided, there is no definitively correct answer. However, if one *must* be chosen, it would be CPT 60210. The question states "partial thyroidectomy" without any details. CPT 60210 is for the partial removal of only one lobe.

**Research Note:**

The question lacks key details, making definitive coding impossible. To accurately code a partial thyroidectomy, one must know: 1) How much of the thyroid gland was removed. 2) Was a portion of one lobe removed? 3) Was a portion of both lobes removed? 4) Was the isthmus removed? Without these details, the selection of a code is arbitrary. The ICD-10 code for hyperthyroidism is E05, with several subcategories offering more specificity.

## Question 86 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: According to Medicare, the "Three-Day Payment Window Rule" refers to:

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
Option B, 'Services provided to a patient 3 days prior to their inpatient admission,' accurately describes Medicare's Three-Day Payment Window Rule. This rule dictates that certain outpatient services provided by a hospital (or wholly owned entity) within three days (or one day for some facilities) prior to an inpatient admission are bundled into the inpatient claim to prevent duplicate payments. The other options are incorrect as they relate to different aspects of billing, claim processing, or patient rights unrelated to this specific rule.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the "Three-Day Payment Window Rule" according to Medicare and evaluate the provided options based on 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines.

Based on the research, here's an analysis of the options:

*   **Core Concept:** The "Three-Day Payment Window Rule" as it pertains to Medicare.
*   **Correct Answer:** B: Services provided to a patient 3 days prior to their inpatient admission.

**Explanation of Options:**

*   **A: 'The time frame in which a patient must pay their bill' - INCORRECT.** The Three-Day Payment Window Rule doesn't dictate when a patient must pay their bill. It concerns how Medicare reimburses hospitals for certain services.
*   **B: 'Services provided to a patient 3 days prior to their inpatient admission' - CORRECT.** This option accurately describes the core of the rule. Medicare's Three-Day (or One-Day) Payment Window requires that certain outpatient services (diagnostic and related non-diagnostic) provided by a hospital (or an entity wholly owned or operated by the hospital) within three days prior to an inpatient admission be included on the hospital's inpatient claim. This applies to hospitals paid under the Inpatient Prospective Payment System (IPPS). A one-day window applies to facilities exempt from IPPS.
*   **C: 'The time frame in which Medicare must process a claim' - INCORRECT.** This describes a completely different process related to claim processing timelines, not the payment bundling rule.
*   **D: 'The period within which a patient can dispute a charge' - INCORRECT.** This refers to patient rights and appeal processes, unrelated to the Three-Day Payment Window Rule.

**Research Note:**

The Three-Day Payment Window rule has been in effect since at least 2010, stemming from the "Preservation of Access to Care for Medicare Beneficiaries and Pension Relief Act of 2010". The rule's purpose is to prevent duplicate payments for services rendered close to the time of inpatient admission. CMS continues to update and refine policies related to this rule, as evidenced by the FY 2026 IPPS Final Rule. There are some exceptions to the rule. For example, Rural Health Clinics (RHCs) and Federally Qualified Health Centers (FQHCs) are not subject to the three-day window. Additionally, a demonstration is being implemented from 2026-2030 waiving the three-day rule for beneficiaries who have one of five surgical procedures.
_

## Question 87 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: In ICD-10-CM, how should unspecified codes be utilized?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
The ICD-10-CM Official Guidelines state that unspecified codes should be used only when the documentation doesn't provide more specific information. Therefore, option B is the correct answer.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the ICD-10-CM guidelines regarding the use of unspecified codes and evaluate the provided options.

**1. Core Procedure/Diagnosis:**

The question pertains to the appropriate utilization of "unspecified codes" within the ICD-10-CM coding system. This relates to diagnostic coding rather than a specific procedure.

**2. Verification of Options Against ICD-10-CM Guidelines:**

I will use search queries to find the official ICD-10-CM guidelines on unspecified codes.

Based on the search results, here's what I found regarding the use of unspecified codes in ICD-10-CM:

*   **Official Guidance:** The ICD-10-CM Official Guidelines for Coding and Reporting, updated for FY 2026, emphasizes the importance of accurate and complete documentation. These guidelines are updated annually and coders should use the most current guidelines.
*   **When to Use Unspecified Codes:** "Codes titled 'unspecified' are for use when the information in the medical record is insufficient to assign a more specific code". In ICD-10, unspecified codes should be used as a last resort.
*   **Specificity is Key:** ICD-10-CM has significantly more codes than ICD-9, promoting a more precise coding system. Therefore, strive to use the most specific code possible.
*   **Potential for Claim Issues:** Using unspecified codes when more specific information is available can lead to claim denials and rejections.
*   **Importance of Documentation:** Accurate coding relies on thorough documentation. A joint effort between healthcare providers and coders is essential.
*   **Querying the Provider:** When documentation is unclear, query the provider for more specific information.
*   **Unspecified vs. Other Specified:** An "unspecified" code indicates that the condition was unknown during diagnosis, while "other specified" means a more specific code exists, but doesn't cover the patient's condition.

**3. Evaluation of Options:**

*   **A: 'Frequently; as they are easy to use' - Incorrect.** This is incorrect. The guidelines emphasize specificity, and unspecified codes should only be used when detailed information is lacking.
*   **B: 'Only when the documentation doesn't provide more specific information' - Correct.** This aligns with the official ICD-10-CM guidelines. Unspecified codes are intended for situations where the available documentation is insufficient to assign a more precise code.
*   **C: 'When the coder is unsure about the specifics of the condition' - Incorrect.** The coder should query the physician for clarification if unsure. Unspecified codes are not a substitute for incomplete coding.
*   **D: 'In any situation where a quick code is needed' - Incorrect.** This is incorrect. Accuracy and specificity are paramount, not speed.

**4. Deleted Codes:**

The search results mention that the FY 2026 ICD-10-CM update includes the removal of 28 codes. However, there is no information about specific deleted codes related to "unspecified" conditions, nor a way to determine the "content match strength" as requested. To identify deleted codes that previously related to the concept of "unspecified," one would need access to the full list of code changes and their definitions from prior years, and then compare the definitions to the question text.

**5. Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The ICD-10-CM coding system prioritizes specificity. Unspecified codes are acceptable *only* when the medical record lacks the necessary details to assign a more precise code. Coders should not use unspecified codes simply for convenience or when unsure; instead, they should seek clarification from the provider. The increasing emphasis on data quality means payers are scrutinizing unspecified codes more closely, potentially leading to claim denials if more specific codes could have been used.

**Final Answer:**

The correct answer is **B: Only when the documentation doesn't provide more specific information.**

_Okay, I will research the CPT code for cystography, considering the 2026 guidelines and the provided options.

Okay, here's my analysis of the CPT codes for Sophia's cystography:

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is a cystography performed to investigate recurrent UTIs. A cystography is an X-ray of the bladder, often involving the injection of contrast dye via a catheter to visualize the bladder. The purpose is to diagnose problems in the bladder.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions:**

*   **A: 50395** - Introduction of guide into renal pelvis and/or ureter with dilation to establish nephrostomy tract, percutaneous. This code was deleted in 2019. In 2022, two new codes (50436 and 50437) replaced 50395 to report access for subsequent endourologic procedures. 50436 is reported when there is an existing nephrostomy tube, and 50437 is reported when there is no existing nephrostomy tube.
*   **B: 50250** - Open cryosurgical ablation of one or more renal mass lesions, including ultrasound guidance and monitoring during the procedure. This involves using extreme cold to destroy abnormal tissue on the kidney.
*   **C: 50200** - Renal biopsy; percutaneous by trocar or needle. This is a procedure where a needle is inserted into the kidney to collect a tissue sample.
*   **D: 51600** - Injection procedure for cystography or voiding urethrocystography. It requires the placement of a urinary catheter.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

CPT code 50395 was deleted in January 1, 2019. The definition was: Introduction of guide into renal pelvis and/or ureter with dilation to establish nephrostomy tract, percutaneous.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

The content match strength for code 50395 is **LOW**. The definition of 50395 relates to establishing a nephrostomy tract, which is not relevant to a cystography.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 50395** - **Incorrect**. This code was deleted in 2019, and its definition does not match the cystography procedure described in the question.
*   **B: 50250** - **Incorrect**. This code is for cryosurgical ablation of renal lesions, which is a completely different procedure than cystography.
*   **C: 50200** - **Incorrect**. This code describes a renal biopsy, which is also a different procedure than cystography.
*   **D: 51600** - **Correct**. This code accurately describes the injection procedure for cystography, which involves injecting contrast into the bladder.

**Research Note:**

The key to this question is understanding the definition of cystography. The procedure involves injecting contrast into the bladder for X-ray imaging. CPT code 51600 specifically describes the injection procedure for cystography. Options A, B, and C describe procedures related to the kidney, not the bladder, and are therefore incorrect. Also, CPT 50395 is a deleted code.

## Question 89 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: In CPT coding, what does a modifier -25 indicate?

**Selected**: D
**Correct Answer**: D
**Rationale**:
Modifier -25 indicates a 'Significant and separately identifiable evaluation and management service by the same physician on the same day of the procedure'. This aligns precisely with the definition provided in CPT coding guidelines, signifying that the patient's condition warranted an E/M service that was distinct and significant from the procedure performed. Options A, B, and C relate to different modifiers or general coding concepts and are not accurate representations of modifier -25's purpose.

**Research Notes**:
_Here's an analysis of the CPT modifier -25 and the provided answer options:

**1. Core Procedure/Diagnosis:**

The question concerns the definition and appropriate use of CPT modifier -25. This modifier is related to Evaluation and Management (E/M) services and their relationship to other procedures performed on the same day.

**2. Verification of Options:**

*   **A: 'Repeat procedure by the same physician'** - Incorrect. Modifier -25 does not relate to repeat procedures.
*   **B: 'Bilateral procedure'** - Incorrect. Bilateral procedures are indicated by modifier -50.
*   **C: 'Multiple procedures'** - Incorrect. While multiple procedures may occur on the same day, modifier -25 specifically addresses the relationship between an E/M service and another procedure, not multiple procedures in general.
*   **D: 'Significant and separately identifiable evaluation and management service by the same physician on the same day of the procedure'** - Correct. This is the exact definition of modifier -25. It indicates that the patient's condition required a significant E/M service that was distinct from the procedure performed.

**3. Deleted Codes:**

This question does not involve deleted codes.

**4. Content Match Strength:**

Not applicable.

**5. Explanation of Correct/Incorrect Options:**

*   **A:** Incorrect because modifier -25 is not used to report repeat procedures.
*   **B:** Incorrect because modifier -25 is not used to indicate bilateral procedures.
*   **C:** Incorrect because modifier -25 doesn't simply mean multiple procedures were performed. It highlights a specific relationship between an E/M service and another procedure.
*   **D:** Correct because it accurately reflects the CPT definition of modifier -25, which signifies that a separately identifiable E/M service was performed on the same day as another procedure. This E/M service must be significant and distinct from the usual work associated with the procedure.

**Research Note:**

Modifier -25 is a frequently misunderstood modifier. It's crucial to remember that it's appended to the E/M code, not the procedure code. It indicates that the E/M service was significant and separately identifiable from the procedure. Proper documentation is essential to support the use of this modifier. The E/M service must be above and beyond the typical pre- or post-operative care associated with the procedure.

## Question 90 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: What does the term "cardiomyopathy" refer to?

**Selected**: C
**Correct Answer**: C
**Rationale**:
The research clearly states that cardiomyopathy is a disease of the heart muscle. Option A refers to myocarditis, option B describes a possible consequence but not the definition, and option D refers to coronary artery disease. Therefore, option C is the correct answer.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about cardiomyopathy, using the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines and provide a detailed explanation.

**1. Core Diagnosis:** Cardiomyopathy

**2. Verification of Options:**

To determine the correct answer, I will research the definition of "cardiomyopathy" and related terms.

Based on the search results:

*   **Core Definition:** Cardiomyopathy is a disease of the heart muscle. It weakens the heart muscle, making it harder for the heart to pump blood to the rest of the body. It can cause the heart muscle to become enlarged, thick, or rigid.

*   **ICD-10 Code:** I42 is the main code for cardiomyopathy. The 2026 edition of ICD-10-CM code I42 became effective on October 1, 2025. I42 should not be used for reimbursement purposes, as there are more detailed codes available. Specific types of cardiomyopathy have their own codes (e.g., I42.1 for obstructive hypertrophic cardiomyopathy, I42.7 for cardiomyopathy due to drug and external agent, I42.8 for other cardiomyopathies, and I42.9 for unspecified cardiomyopathy).

*   **CPT Codes:** There were changes to CPT codes for 2026, especially in interventional cardiology and vascular procedures. However, none of the updates directly define cardiomyopathy.

**3. & 4. Deleted Codes Research:**

*   CPT codes 92975 and 92977 (for intracoronary thrombolytic infusion therapy during catheterization) were deleted in 2026 because they were rarely utilized.
*   CPT codes 37220-37235 were deleted and replaced with 46 new codes. The new codes (37254-37299) are for LER services that are performed percutaneously and/or through open surgical exposure for occlusive disease.
*   CPT codes 75956–75959 were deleted in 2026. These represented imaging supervision/interpretation for certain endovascular aortic repair extensions, which have been bundled into primary surgical codes or made obsolete by new endograft technology.

**Content Match Strength for Deleted Codes:** The definitions of the deleted codes do *not* directly match the question about the definition of "cardiomyopathy."

**5. Explanation of Options:**

*   **A: Inflammation of the heart muscle:** Incorrect. Inflammation of the heart muscle is *myocarditis*, not cardiomyopathy.
*   **B: Enlargement of the heart:** Incorrect. While cardiomyopathy can *cause* enlargement of the heart (cardiomegaly or dilated cardiomyopathy), the term itself refers to a broader category of heart muscle diseases.
*   **C: Disease of the heart muscle:** Correct. This is the most accurate and comprehensive definition of cardiomyopathy.
*   **D: Blockage in the heart's arteries:** Incorrect. This refers to coronary artery disease or atherosclerosis, not cardiomyopathy.

**Research Note:**

The correct answer is C. Cardiomyopathy is a general term for diseases affecting the heart muscle. While some types of cardiomyopathy can lead to heart enlargement, the core definition focuses on the heart muscle itself. The ICD-10 code I42 is the primary code, with more specific subcodes for different types. CPT code changes for 2026 do not affect the definition of cardiomyopathy.

**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
J1745 is the correct HCPCS Level II code for Remicade (infliximab), excluding biosimilars, dosed per 10 mg. J1750 is for iron dextran, J1756 is for iron sucrose, and no reliable source suggests J1760 is for Remicade.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the HCPCS Level II code for Remicade infusion, considering the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines.

*   The core procedure is the intravenous infusion of Remicade (infliximab) for Crohn's disease.

**2. Code Verification:**

*   **A: J1745 - Injection, infliximab, excludes biosimilar, 10 mg**
    *   This is the correct HCPCS Level II code for Remicade (infliximab). It represents 10 mg of infliximab. Billing is done in units of 10 mg.
*   **B: J1750 - Injection, iron dextran, 50 mg**
    *   This code is for iron dextran, not infliximab (Remicade).
*   **C: J1756 - Injection, iron sucrose, per 1 mg**
    *   This code is for iron sucrose (Venofer), not infliximab (Remicade).
*   **D: J1760**
    *   I could not find any reliable sources that mentioned what J1760 refers to.

**3. Deleted Codes:**
Based on the search results, none of the provided codes appear to be deleted for 2026.

**4. Content Match Strength for Deleted Codes:**
*   Not applicable, as no codes are identified as deleted.

**5. Explanation of Correct/Incorrect Options:**

*   **A: J1745 - Correct.** This is the specific HCPCS Level II code assigned to infliximab (Remicade), excluding biosimilars, dosed per 10 mg.
*   **B: J1750 - Incorrect.** This code is for iron dextran, a completely different medication than infliximab (Remicade).
*   **C: J1756 - Incorrect.** This code is for iron sucrose, not infliximab (Remicade).
*   **D: J1760 - Incorrect.** There is no information available to suggest that this code is used for Remicade.

**Research Note:**

The correct HCPCS Level II code for Remicade (infliximab) infusion is J1745. Remember that the quantity billed should reflect the total milligrams of infliximab administered, with each unit of J1745 representing 10 mg. Also, remember to use the appropriate CPT codes for the infusion service itself (e.g., 96413, 96415, 96365, 96366).

## Question 93 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: When it comes to Medicare fraud and abuse, what does "upcoding" refer to?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
The correct answer is B: Billing a higher service code than what was performed. Upcoding is a specific type of medical billing fraud where providers intentionally use codes that represent more complex or expensive services than those actually rendered to receive higher reimbursements. Option A refers to billing for services not rendered, which is a different type of fraud. Option C refers to billing for unnecessary services, which is also a separate type of fraud. Option D is the opposite of upcoding.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about Medicare fraud and abuse, specifically focusing on the definition of "upcoding." I will use the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines as context, verify each option, explain why each option is correct or incorrect, and provide a research note.

### Analysis of Options:

*   **A: Billing for services not rendered:** This describes a different type of fraud, where a provider bills for services that were never performed. This is not "upcoding".
*   **B: Billing a higher service code than what was performed:** This accurately defines upcoding. It involves using a code that represents a more complex or expensive service than what was actually provided.
*   **C: Billing for unnecessary services:** This is another distinct type of fraud, where a provider bills for services that were not medically necessary for the patient's condition.
*   **D: Assigning a lower code to save the patient money:** This is the opposite of upcoding. While it might seem beneficial to the patient, it can still be problematic as it misrepresents the services provided.

### Conclusion:

The correct answer is **B: Billing a higher service code than what was performed.** Upcoding is a specific type of medical billing fraud where providers intentionally use codes that represent more complex or expensive services than those actually rendered to receive higher reimbursements.

**Research Note:**
Upcoding is a prevalent form of healthcare fraud that involves submitting inaccurate CPT codes to obtain higher reimbursements. This practice violates the False Claims Act and can lead to significant financial losses for Medicare and taxpayers.
_
---
## Question 94 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Max complained of fatigue and frequent infections. His doctor ordered an immunoglobulin test to check his immune system's health. Which CPT code corresponds to the immunoglobulin test?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
While CPT 82785 is a plausible alternative if the doctor ordered an IgE test, CPT 82784 is the better fit because the question mentions a general immunoglobulin test to check the immune system's health and does not specify IgE. Options B and D are invalid CPT codes, so they are incorrect.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the immunoglobulin test and provide a detailed explanation for each option.

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is an immunoglobulin test to assess the patient's immune system health due to complaints of fatigue and frequent infections.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use the available tools to search for the definitions of the provided CPT codes.

**3. Option Analysis:**

*   **A: 82784 - Immunoglobulin (IgA, IgD, IgG, IgM), each**. This code is used to report the measurement of individual immunoglobulin classes (IgA, IgD, IgG, or IgM) in serum or plasma. It is appropriate when each immunoglobulin class is measured separately and is medically necessary for diagnosis, monitoring, or treatment planning. The clinical indications for this code include evaluation of suspected immunodeficiencies, monitoring immunoglobulin therapy, diagnosis and follow-up of autoimmune disorders, and assessment of infection risk or recurrent infections. Given the patient's fatigue and frequent infections, this is a strong contender, assuming the doctor ordered individual measurements of IgA, IgD, IgG, or IgM.
*   **B: 82782 -** No clear definition found. There may be a typo in the option. I am unable to locate a valid CPT code 82782 for immunoglobulin testing.
*   **C: 82785 - Gammaglobulin (immunoglobulin); IgE**. This code is used to report the measurement of Immunoglobulin E (IgE). It is often associated with allergy testing. While fatigue and frequent infections *can* be related to allergies, the question specifies a general immunoglobulin test to check the immune system's health, not specifically an IgE test for allergies. If the doctor ordered an IgE test, this code would be appropriate.
*   **D: 82783** - No clear definition found. There may be a typo in the option. I am unable to locate a valid CPT code 82783 for immunoglobulin testing.

**4. Deleted Codes Research:**
I could not find evidence that any of these codes have been deleted.

**5. Explanation of Correct or Incorrect Options:**

*   **A: 82784 - Correct** (Potentially). This is the most likely correct answer if the doctor ordered individual quantitative measurements of IgA, IgD, IgG, or IgM. The patient's symptoms align with potential immune system issues that this test could help diagnose.
*   **B: 82782 - Incorrect.** There is no valid CPT code 82782 for immunoglobulin testing.
*   **C: 82785 - Correct** (Potentially). This could be correct if the physician specifically ordered an IgE test, perhaps suspecting an allergic component to the patient's fatigue and infections. However, without specific mention of allergy, it's less likely than 82784.
*   **D: 82783 - Incorrect.** There is no valid CPT code 82783 for immunoglobulin testing.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The key to selecting the correct code is determining *exactly* what type of immunoglobulin test was ordered.

*   If the test was for individual IgA, IgD, IgG, or IgM levels, then CPT code 82784 is the most accurate choice.
*   If the test was specifically for IgE (allergy testing), then CPT code 82785 would be correct.

Because the question states, "immunoglobulin test to check his immune system's health," without specifying IgE, 82784 is *slightly* more likely. However, CPT 82785 is a plausible alternative. Both CPT 82782 and 82783 seem to be coding errors in the answer options.

## Question 95 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: When a patient is admitted to the hospital for a high fever and is later diagnosed with sepsis, what should be the primary diagnosis according to ICD-10-CM guidelines?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
ICD-10-CM guidelines state that if a patient is admitted with sepsis, the code for sepsis should be sequenced first. Although the patient presented with fever, the definitive diagnosis is sepsis, making it the primary diagnosis. The other options are not in accordance with ICD-10-CM guidelines for sequencing the primary diagnosis in this scenario.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about a patient admitted with a high fever and later diagnosed with sepsis, focusing on the appropriate primary diagnosis according to ICD-10-CM guidelines for 2026.

**Question:** When a patient is admitted to the hospital for a high fever and is later diagnosed with sepsis, what should be the primary diagnosis according to ICD-10-CM guidelines?
Options: {'A': 'Fever', 'B': 'Sepsis', 'C': 'Both can be primary', 'D': 'The condition that prompted the admission'}

Here's my plan:

1.  **Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:** The core issue is determining the correct primary diagnosis code in ICD-10-CM when a patient presents with fever and is subsequently diagnosed with sepsis.
2.  **Verify each option against ICD-10-CM guidelines (current and historical):** I will use search queries to find information on ICD-10-CM guidelines regarding sepsis and fever as primary diagnoses, specifically looking for guidance on sequencing.
3.  **If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION:** Not applicable in this case, as we are dealing with diagnostic *guidelines*, not specific code deletions.
4.  **CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?:** Not applicable.
5.  **Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect:** I'll provide a rationale based on the ICD-10-CM guidelines.

Based on the search results, here's the breakdown of the options:

*   **A: Fever** - Incorrect. While the patient presented with a fever, it led to the discovery and diagnosis of sepsis. Coding guidelines emphasize coding the underlying systemic infection (sepsis) as the principal diagnosis when it's present on admission.  Fever (R50.9 or R50.81) may be assigned if no definitive diagnosis is available. In this case, sepsis *is* the definitive diagnosis.
*   **B: Sepsis** - Correct.  ICD-10-CM guidelines state that if a patient is admitted with sepsis, the code for sepsis should be sequenced first. Code A41.9 (Sepsis, unspecified organism) may be used if the specific organism is not documented.
*   **C: Both can be primary** - Incorrect. ICD-10-CM guidelines provide specific instructions for sequencing diagnoses, and in this case, sepsis takes precedence as the primary diagnosis.
*   **D: The condition that prompted the admission** - Incorrect. While fever prompted the admission, the underlying *definitive* condition is sepsis. If the patient was admitted with a localized infection *that then progressed to sepsis*, the localized infection would be coded first. However, the question states the patient was *diagnosed* with sepsis, implying it was present or suspected at admission.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The ICD-10-CM coding guidelines are very specific regarding the sequencing of sepsis. When sepsis is diagnosed in a patient admitted with related symptoms like fever, sepsis should be coded as the primary diagnosis. This is consistent across multiple sources referencing the official guidelines. The guidelines prioritize identifying and coding the underlying systemic infection.

## Question 96 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Jason went to the clinic after noticing a sore that wouldn't heal inside his mouth. The doctor performed an excision of the oral lesion. Which CPT code represents this procedure?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
Code 41110 (Excision Procedures on the Tongue and Floor of Mouth) is the most appropriate choice. While the question only specifies an 'oral lesion' and doesn't explicitly state 'tongue lesion,' 41110 is the most specific active code for excising a lesion *inside* the mouth, which aligns better than the other options. Code 41108 is for biopsy, not excision. Code 40100 was not found. Code 40819 is for the vestibule of the mouth (lips/cheeks) and thus anatomically incorrect. Therefore, 41110 is the best fit based on the available information and the test-bank heuristic to prioritize the best anatomical site when an exact match is missing.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about the excision of an oral lesion, following the provided guidelines.

**1. Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:**

The core procedure is the excision of an oral lesion.

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

I will use the available tools to look up the definitions of the provided CPT codes.

Based on the search results:

*   **41108:** Excision Procedures on the Tongue and Floor of Mouth - In this procedure, the provider performs an incision in the floor of the mouth and excises tissue for the purpose of biopsy. It can also be for diagnostic purposes to evaluate conditions such as infections, lesions, or cancer.
*   **41110:** Excision Procedures on the Tongue and Floor of Mouth - In this procedure, the provider makes an incision in the tongue and excises the lesion from the tongue. This procedure involves the removal of an abnormal growth or lesion on the tongue. It is typically performed without stitching the wound closed and allows the site to heal naturally.
*   **40100:** This code was not found in the search results.
*   **40819:** Excision and Destruction Procedures on the Vestibule of Mouth - In this procedure, the provider removes the labial or buccal frenum, each of which is a membrane structure in the mouth. Labial refers to the lip and buccal refers to the cheek. This procedure is typically performed to address cosmetic concerns or to treat conditions that may affect the appearance or function of the mouth and surrounding tissues.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

Based on the search results, none of the codes appear to be deleted.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable, as no codes were deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: 41108 - Incorrect.** This code is for a *biopsy* of the floor of the mouth, not a complete excision of a lesion. The question specifies an excision, implying complete removal, not just a sample.
*   **B: 41110 - Correct.** This code describes the excision of a lesion of the tongue. This aligns with the scenario where the doctor performed an excision of an oral lesion.
*   **C: 40100 - Incorrect.** This code's definition could not be found, making it impossible to confirm if it is correct.
*   **D: 40819 - Incorrect.** This code is for the excision of a frenum (labial or buccal) in the vestibule of the mouth (lip or cheek area). The question refers to a general "oral lesion," not specifically a frenum.

**Research Note:**

The key to this question is differentiating between a biopsy and an excision. Code 41108 is specifically for a *biopsy* of the floor of the mouth. Code 41110 is a better fit because it describes the excision of a lesion on the tongue without closure, aligning with the doctor's procedure to remove the oral lesion. The location of the lesion, described as being "inside his mouth", most closely aligns with the tongue. Code 40819 is incorrect as it specifies the vestibule of the mouth.

## Question 97 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Nancy was fitted with a below-the-knee artificial limb after her leg amputation. Which HCPCS Level II code represents this prosthetic?

**Selected**: B
**Correct Answer**: B
**Rationale**:
The question asks for the HCPCS Level II code for a below-the-knee artificial limb fitting. While both L5637 and L5645 describe additions to a below-knee prosthesis, the question implies there is a single best answer. L5637 (Addition to lower extremity, below knee, total contact) is chosen because it describes a basic addition to a below-knee prosthesis. L5645 is more specific describing 'flexible inner socket, external frame'. Without further details, L5637 is more likely the general code for a BK prosthesis addition, making it the best fit according to test-taking logic when one code is explicitly requested.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the HCPCS Level II code for a below-the-knee artificial limb fitting, following the provided guidelines.

Here's my analysis of the HCPCS Level II codes for a below-the-knee artificial limb:

**1. Core Procedure/Diagnosis:** Fitting a below-the-knee (BK) artificial limb/prosthesis.

**2. Code Verification:**

*   **L5631:** Addition to lower extremity, above knee or knee disarticulation, acrylic socket. This code describes a socket for an *above*-knee amputation or knee disarticulation, not below the knee.
*   **L5637:** Addition to lower extremity, below knee, total contact. This code describes an addition to a *below*-knee prosthesis, specifically a total contact socket.
*   **L5645:** Addition to lower extremity, below knee, flexible inner socket, external frame. This code describes an addition to a *below*-knee prosthesis, using a flexible inner socket with an external frame.
*   **L5650:** Additions to lower extremity, total contact, above knee or knee disarticulation socket. This code is for *above*-knee or knee disarticulation prostheses, not below the knee.

**3. Deleted Codes:**

*   Based on the search results, none of the codes appear to be deleted for 2026. CMS releases updates to HCPCS Level II codes quarterly, so it's important to use the most current information.

**4. Content Match Strength (for potential deleted codes):**  N/A

**5. Explanation:**

*   **L5631 (Incorrect):** This code is for above-knee or knee disarticulation prostheses, not below-knee.
*   **L5637 (Correct):** This accurately describes an addition to a below-knee prosthesis involving a total contact socket.
*   **L5645 (Correct):** This accurately describes an addition to a below-knee prosthesis involving a flexible inner socket and external frame.
*   **L5650 (Incorrect):** This code is for above-knee or knee disarticulation prostheses, not below-knee.

**Research Note:**

The question asks for *the* HCPCS Level II code, implying a single correct answer. However, both L5637 and L5645 describe below-knee additions. L5637 specifies "total contact," while L5645 specifies "flexible inner socket, external frame."  Without more information about the *specific* type of below-knee prosthetic fitting Nancy received, *both* L5637 and L5645 are potentially correct. Evaluators should be aware of this ambiguity. If the question *requires* a single answer, it is flawed.

## Question 98 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Tyler had a lump on his thyroid. The endocrinologist performed a fine needle aspiration biopsy. Which CPT code pertains to this procedure?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
The question asks for the CPT code for a fine needle aspiration biopsy of the thyroid. While 60100 is technically for a core needle biopsy, it is the only biopsy code present in the provided options. Therefore, based on test-taking strategy, 60100 is the best option because it aligns with the procedure type (biopsy) and anatomical location (thyroid), where a more specific FNA code is not present in the options. This aligns with the 'Anatomical Site > Clinical Action' heuristic.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I'll research the medical coding question about the fine needle aspiration biopsy of the thyroid lump, using the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines.

**Question:** Tyler had a lump on his thyroid. The endocrinologist performed a fine needle aspiration biopsy. Which CPT code pertains to this procedure?
Options: {'A': '60100', 'B': '60240', 'C': '60220', 'D': '60212'}

Here's my breakdown:

1.  **Identify the core procedure/diagnosis:** The core procedure is a fine needle aspiration (FNA) biopsy of the thyroid. The diagnosis is a thyroid lump (nodule).

2.  **Verify each option against CPT definitions (current AND historical):**

*   **60100 - Biopsy thyroid, percutaneous core needle**
    *   This code describes a percutaneous core needle biopsy of the thyroid gland.
    *   It involves removing a tissue sample for histological examination.
*   **60240 - Thyroidectomy, total or complete**
    *   This code describes the surgical removal of the entire thyroid gland.
    *   It is used to treat conditions like cancer, hyperthyroidism, and large goiters.
*   **60220 - Total thyroid lobectomy, unilateral; with or without isthmusectomy**
    *   This code represents the complete surgical removal of one lobe of the thyroid gland, with or without removal of the isthmus.
*   **60212 - Partial thyroid lobectomy, unilateral; with contralateral subtotal lobectomy, including isthmusectomy**
    *   This code describes a procedure where a portion of one thyroid lobe is removed along with a subtotal portion of the other lobe and the isthmus.

3.  **If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**
    *   None of the codes appear to be deleted.

4.  **CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**
    *   N/A

5.  **Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

    *   **A: 60100 - Correct.** This is the most accurate code because the question specifically states that a *fine needle aspiration biopsy* was performed. While 60100 is for a *core needle* biopsy, it appears to be the only biopsy code present in the options.
    *   **B: 60240 - Incorrect.** This code is for a total thyroidectomy, which is the removal of the entire thyroid gland. The question specifies a biopsy, not a complete removal.
    *   **C: 60220 - Incorrect.** This code is for the removal of one entire lobe of the thyroid gland (total lobectomy). The question specifies a biopsy, not a lobectomy.
    *   **D: 60212 - Incorrect.** This code is for the partial removal of one lobe and a subtotal removal of the other lobe. The question specifies a biopsy, not a partial or subtotal removal.

**Research Note:**

The question asks for the CPT code for a *fine needle aspiration* biopsy. However, code 60100 refers to a *core needle* biopsy. Despite this discrepancy, 60100 is the only biopsy code provided in the options, making it the most appropriate choice. Ideally, the options would include a CPT code specifically for FNA, such as codes in the range 10005-10012. If ultrasound guidance was used, code 76942 could be added.

## Question 99 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Lily felt a sudden blockage in her nose. The doctor diagnosed a deviated septum and recommended a septoplasty. Which CPT code pertains to this procedure?

**Selected**: D
**Correct Answer**: D
**Rationale**:
Code 30520 is the correct CPT code for septoplasty, the surgical repair of a deviated nasal septum. The other options describe unrelated procedures, such as diagnostic endoscopy (31231), maxillary sinus irrigation (31000), and partial ethmoidectomy (31254). Therefore, option D is the most accurate.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the medical coding question about septoplasty, providing detailed analysis and reasoning for each CPT code option.

**Question:** Lily felt a sudden blockage in her nose. The doctor diagnosed a deviated septum and recommended a septoplasty. Which CPT code pertains to this procedure?
Options: {'A': '31231', 'B': '31000', 'C': '31254', 'D': '30520'}

**1. Identify the Core Procedure/Diagnosis:**

*   **Core Procedure:** Septoplasty (surgical repair of the nasal septum)
*   **Diagnosis:** Deviated Septum

**2. Verify each option against CPT/ICD definitions (current AND historical):**

*   **A: 31231 - Nasal endoscopy, diagnostic, unilateral or bilateral (separate procedure)**. This code is for a diagnostic procedure where an endoscope is used to examine the nasal passages. It is *not* for a surgical procedure like septoplasty.
*   **B: 31000 - Lavage by cannulation; maxillary sinus (antrum puncture or natural ostium)**. This code describes irrigating the maxillary sinus to clear blockages. It does not describe a septoplasty.
*   **C: 31254 - Nasal/sinus endoscopy, surgical; with ethmoidectomy, partial (anterior)**. This code is for a *partial ethmoidectomy* performed with a nasal endoscope. An ethmoidectomy involves removing tissue from the ethmoid sinuses. This is different from a septoplasty, which involves correcting the nasal septum.
*   **D: 30520 - Septoplasty or submucous resection, with or without cartilage scoring, contouring or replacement with graft**. This code accurately describes a septoplasty, which is performed to correct a deviated nasal septum. The procedure may involve scoring, contouring, or replacing cartilage.

**3. If a code is DELETED, research WHEN it was deleted and the DEFINITION.**

None of the codes appear to be deleted. All are currently active CPT codes.

**4. CRITICAL: Report the "CONTENT MATCH STRENGTH" for deleted codes. Does the OLD definition match the question text EXACTLY?**

Not applicable, as no codes are deleted.

**5. Explain WHY each option is Correct OR Incorrect.**

*   **A: Incorrect.** Code 31231 is for *diagnostic* nasal endoscopy, not septoplasty. The question describes a surgical procedure (septoplasty) to correct a diagnosed condition (deviated septum), not a diagnostic examination.
*   **B: Incorrect.** Code 31000 is for irrigating the maxillary sinus. This is unrelated to septoplasty, which focuses on the nasal septum.
*   **C: Incorrect.** Code 31254 describes a partial ethmoidectomy, a sinus surgery, not a septoplasty. The ethmoid sinuses are different anatomical structures than the nasal septum.
*   **D: Correct.** Code 30520 is the correct CPT code for septoplasty, the surgical repair of a deviated nasal septum.

**Research Note for the Evaluator:**

The question clearly describes a septoplasty procedure. The correct answer, CPT code 30520, directly corresponds to this procedure. The other options describe unrelated procedures, such as diagnostic endoscopy (31231), maxillary sinus irrigation (31000), and partial ethmoidectomy (31254). The context provided specifies 2026 CPT guidelines, and the analysis confirms that code 30520 remains the appropriate code for septoplasty in the current year.

## Question 100 - ✅ CORRECT
**Question**: Anna received an injection of Botox for her chronic migraines. Which HCPCS Level II code represents the Botox injection?

**Selected**: A
**Correct Answer**: A
**Rationale**:
J0585 is the correct HCPCS Level II code for the injection of Botox (onabotulinumtoxinA). The research clearly states this, and the question asks specifically for the code representing Botox. While other options represent different botulinum toxins, J0585 directly corresponds to the brand name 'Botox'.

**Research Notes**:
_Okay, I will research the HCPCS Level II code for Botox injections for chronic migraines, considering the 2026 CPT and ICD-10 guidelines.

Here's the breakdown of the HCPCS Level II codes for Botox injections, specifically in the context of chronic migraines:

**1. Core Procedure/Diagnosis:**

*   The core procedure is the injection of botulinum toxin.
*   The diagnosis is chronic migraines.

**2. Code Verification:**

*   **J0585: Injection, onabotulinumtoxinA, 1 unit (Botox)**
    *   This code represents the injection of OnabotulinumtoxinA, which is the specific type of botulinum toxin used in Botox.
    *   Botox is often used in the treatment of chronic migraines.
*   **J0586: Injection, abobotulinumtoxinA, 5 units (Dysport)**
    *   This code represents the injection of AbobotulinumtoxinA, which is the specific type of botulinum toxin used in Dysport.
    *   Dysport is sometimes used for chronic migraines.
*   **J0587: Injection, rimabotulinumtoxinB, 100 units (Myobloc)**
    *   This code represents the injection of RimabotulinumtoxinB, which is the specific type of botulinum toxin used in Myobloc.
    *   Myobloc has more limited use for migraines compared to Botox and Xeomin.
*   **J0588: Injection, incobotulinumtoxinA, 1 unit (Xeomin)**
    *   This code represents the injection of Incobotulinumtoxin A, which is the specific type of botulinum toxin used in Xeomin.
    *   Xeomin is sometimes used off-label for chronic migraines.

**3. Deleted Codes:**

*   None of the codes appear to be deleted. All are active for 2025 and 2026.

**4. Content Match Strength (for potentially deleted codes):**

*   Not applicable, as none of the codes are deleted.

**5. Explanation of Correct/Incorrect Options:**

*   **A: J0585 - Correct.** J0585 is the correct code for Botox (onabotulinumtoxinA), which is a common treatment for chronic migraines.
*   **B: J0586 - Incorrect.** J0586 is the code for Dysport (abobotulinumtoxinA). While Dysport is a botulinum toxin, the question specifically asks for the code representing *Botox*.
*   **C: J0587 - Incorrect.** J0587 is the code for Myobloc (rimabotulinumtoxinB). Myobloc is a botulinum toxin, but not the one typically associated with migraine treatment.
*   **D: J0588 - Incorrect.** J0588 is the code for Xeomin (incobotulinumtoxinA). While Xeomin can be used for chronic migraines, the question specifically asks for the code representing *Botox*.

**Research Note for Evaluator:**

The question asks for the HCPCS Level II code that represents the *Botox* injection. While other botulinum toxins (Dysport, Xeomin, Myobloc) may be used for migraine treatment, the most direct and accurate answer is J0585, which corresponds specifically to Botox (onabotulinumtoxinA).
